You MUST use the Sourcegraph MCP tools (keyword_search, finder, list_files, read_file, go_to_definition, find_references, deepsearch, deepsearch_read) to explore and understand this codebase. You are REQUIRED to use these tools extensively — they are your primary means of code discovery.

Sourcegraph repository: `github.com/prometheus/prometheus` (use `repo:^github.com/prometheus/prometheus$` filter in keyword_search)

**REQUIRED WORKFLOW:**
1. FIRST use Sourcegraph tools (keyword_search, finder, list_files) to explore the codebase structure and find relevant code
2. Use go_to_definition and find_references to trace code relationships
3. After finding code via Sourcegraph, use Read to verify actual local contents before editing
4. If Sourcegraph shows different code than local, TRUST THE LOCAL CODE
5. Use `deepsearch` for complex architectural questions — it returns a polling link, NOT immediate results
6. After calling `deepsearch`, continue working with other tools for 30-60 seconds, then call `deepsearch_read` with the polling link
7. Retry `deepsearch_read` at least 3 times (Deep Search takes 50-120 seconds to complete)

See CLAUDE.md for the complete tool selection guide with detailed usage for each tool.

# Investigation: Remote-Write Queue Resharding Failure

**Repository:** prometheus/prometheus
**Task Type:** Cross-Service Debug (investigation only — no code fixes)

## Scenario

After a Prometheus upgrade, remote-write destinations intermittently stop receiving samples. The issue correlates with target discovery changes — when targets are added or removed, some remote-write shards stall.

Prometheus logs show:
```
level=info msg="Resharding queues" from=4 to=6
level=info msg="Resharding done" numShards=6
```

But after resharding, metrics show some shards have `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` stuck at >0 with no progress.

## Your Task

Investigate the root cause and produce a report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:
1. How remote-write queue resharding works (which files/functions)
2. What changed in the resharding logic recently
3. The specific mechanism causing shards to stall
4. Why the issue is intermittent (timing/race condition)
5. Which metrics or logs would confirm the root cause

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Specific file, function, and mechanism>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of packages/modules impacted>

## Recommendation
<Fix strategy and diagnostic steps>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code fixes
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- Focus on `storage/remote/` package, particularly queue management and shard calculation

  1343→type queue struct {
  1344→	// batchMtx covers operations appending to or publishing the partial batch.
  1345→	batchMtx   sync.Mutex
  1346→	batch      []timeSeries
  1347→	batchQueue chan []timeSeries
  1348→
  1349→	// Since we know there are a limited number of batches out, using a stack
  1350→	// is easy and safe so a sync.Pool is not necessary.
  1351→	// poolMtx covers adding and removing batches from the batchPool.
  1352→	poolMtx   sync.Mutex
  1353→	batchPool [][]timeSeries
  1354→}
  1355→
  1356→type timeSeries struct {
  1357→	seriesLabels   labels.Labels
  1358→	value          float64
  1359→	histogram      *histogram.Histogram
  1360→	floatHistogram *histogram.FloatHistogram
  1361→	metadata       *metadata.Metadata
  1362→	timestamp      int64
  1363→	exemplarLabels labels.Labels
  1364→	// The type of series: sample, exemplar, or histogram.
  1365→	sType seriesType
  1366→}
  1367→
  1368→type seriesType int
  1369→
  1370→const (
  1371→	tSample seriesType = iota
  1372→	tExemplar
  1373→	tHistogram
  1374→	tFloatHistogram
  1375→	tMetadata
  1376→)
  1377→
  1378→func newQueue(batchSize, capacity int) *queue {
  1379→	batches := capacity / batchSize
  1380→	// Always create an unbuffered channel even if capacity is configured to be
  1381→	// less than max_samples_per_send.
  1382→	if batches == 0 {
  1383→		batches = 1
  1384→	}
  1385→	return &queue{
  1386→		batch:      make([]timeSeries, 0, batchSize),
  1387→		batchQueue: make(chan []timeSeries, batches),
  1388→		// batchPool should have capacity for everything in the channel + 1 for
  1389→		// the batch being processed.

  1107→// calculateDesiredShards returns the number of desired shards, which will be
  1108→// the current QueueManager.numShards if resharding should not occur for reasons
  1109→// outlined in this functions implementation. It is up to the caller to reshard, or not,
  1110→// based on the return value.
  1111→func (t *QueueManager) calculateDesiredShards() int {
  1112→	t.dataIn.tick()
  1113→	t.dataOut.tick()
  1114→	t.dataOutDuration.tick()
  1115→
  1116→	// We use the number of incoming samples as a prediction of how much work we
  1117→	// will need to do next iteration.  We add to this any pending samples
  1118→	// (received - send) so we can catch up with any backlog. We use the average
  1119→	// outgoing batch latency to work out how many shards we need.
  1120→	var (
  1121→		dataInRate      = t.dataIn.rate()
  1122→		dataOutRate     = t.dataOut.rate()
  1123→		dataOutDuration = t.dataOutDuration.rate() / float64(time.Second)
  1124→		dataPendingRate = dataInRate - dataOutRate
  1125→		highestSent     = t.metrics.highestSentTimestamp.Get()
  1126→		highestRecv     = t.metrics.highestTimestamp.Get()
  1127→		delay           = highestRecv - highestSent
  1128→		dataPending     = delay * dataInRate
  1129→	)

  1307→// enqueue data (sample or exemplar). If the shard is full, shutting down, or
  1308→// resharding, it will return false; in this case, you should back off and
  1309→// retry. A shard is full when its configured capacity has been reached,
  1310→// specifically, when s.queues[shard] has filled its batchQueue channel and the
  1311→// partial batch has also been filled.
  1312→func (s *shards) enqueue(ref chunks.HeadSeriesRef, data timeSeries) bool {
  1313→	s.mtx.RLock()
  1314→	defer s.mtx.RUnlock()
  1315→	shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))
  1316→	select {
  1317→	case <-s.softShutdown:
  1318→		return false
  1319→	default:
  1320→		appended := s.queues[shard].Append(data)
  1321→		if !appended {
  1322→			return false
  1323→		}
  1324→		switch data.sType {
  1325→		case tSample:
  1326→			s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()
  1327→			s.enqueuedSamples.Inc()
  1328→		case tExemplar:
  1329→			s.qm.metrics.pendingExemplars.Inc()
  1330→			s.enqueuedExemplars.Inc()
  1331→		case tHistogram, tFloatHistogram:
  1332→			s.qm.metrics.pendingHistograms.Inc()
  1333→			s.enqueuedHistograms.Inc()
  1334→		default:
  1335→			return true
  1336→		}
  1337→		s.qm.metrics.highestTimestamp.Set(float64(data.timestamp / 1000))
  1338→		s.qm.dataIn.incr(1)
  1339→		return true

# Prometheus Remote Write Scaling Issue - Issue #17384

## Issue Description

Users upgrading Prometheus from version 3.6.0 to 3.7.1 encountered remote write queue stalling across globally distributed instances. The problematic behavior manifested as:

- Instances lagging behind by over an hour
- Shard count remaining between 3-4 despite adequate resources
- CPU utilization below 20% with 25% memory usage on 16GB instances
- Issue reproducible and consistent across multiple upgrade attempts

## Root Cause Analysis

The core problem stemmed from changes in how `dataIn` metrics were calculated. As identified by team member comments: "by incrementing `dataIn` only within the queue manager or shard as opposed to using the `samplesIn` which was updated via calls to `storage.Commit`, we can't account for a samples scrape rate higher than our max possible samples out rate for a given shard count."

## The Resharding Deadlock Mechanism

The resharding logic depends on comparing incoming versus outgoing data rates. When `dataIn` increments occur only during blocking Append operations at shard capacity, the measured `dataIn` rate becomes artificially capped at the `dataOut` rate. This creates a feedback loop preventing shard scaling:

- High scrape rates exceed current shard capacity
- Blocking calls prevent accurate `dataIn` measurement
- Equal `dataIn`/`dataOut` rates signal no resharding needed
- Queued samples accumulate without triggering shard increases

## Resolution

Pull request #17412 reverted the problematic queue resharding logic changes (specifically PR #17065) to restore 3.6 behavior, unblocking the issue for the 3.7 release branch.

89-assistanttext-
The investigation report has been written to `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

**Key findings:**

Commit `184c7eb` moved `dataIn.incr(1)` from `timestampTracker.Commit()` (which runs unconditionally at scrape time) into `shards.enqueue()` (which only succeeds when queues have capacity). This creates a feedback loop:

1. Queues fill up -> `enqueue()` returns false -> `Append()` blocks in retry loop
2. While blocked, `dataIn` is never incremented (it only increments on **successful** enqueue)
3. `calculateDesiredShards()` sees `dataInRate ≈ dataOutRate` -> no resharding needed
4. Queues stay full -> loop repeats

The same commit also removed `dataDropped`/`dataKeptRatio` (affecting relabel-heavy configs) and moved `highestTimestamp` tracking inside `enqueue()` (so the backlog delay metric also stalls).

This was already reverted on the `release-3.7` branch (commit `6806b68`) but remains on `main` at HEAD.

  "result": "# Prometheus Remote Write Scaling Issue - Issue #17384\n\n## Issue Description\n\nUsers upgrading Prometheus from version 3.6.0 to 3.7.1 encountered remote write queue stalling across globally distributed instances. The problematic behavior manifested as:\n\n- Instances lagging behind by over an hour\n- Shard count remaining between 3-4 despite adequate resources\n- CPU utilization below 20% with 25% memory usage on 16GB instances\n- Issue reproducible and consistent across multiple upgrade attempts\n\n## Root Cause Analysis\n\nThe core problem stemmed from changes in how `dataIn` metrics were calculated. As identified by team member comments: \"by incrementing `dataIn` only within the queue manager or shard as opposed to using the `samplesIn` which was updated via calls to `storage.Commit`, we can't account for a samples scrape rate higher than our max possible samples out rate for a given shard count.\"\n\n## The Resharding Deadlock Mechanism\n\nThe resharding logic depends on comparing incoming versus outgoing data rates. When `dataIn` increments occur only during blocking Append operations at shard capacity, the measured `dataIn` rate becomes artificially capped at the `dataOut` rate. This creates a feedback loop preventing shard scaling:\n\n- High scrape rates exceed current shard capacity\n- Blocking calls prevent accurate `dataIn` measurement\n- Equal `dataIn`/`dataOut` rates signal no resharding needed\n- Queued samples accumulate without triggering shard increases\n\n## Resolution\n\nPull request #17412 reverted the problematic queue resharding logic changes (specifically PR #17065) to restore 3.6 behavior, unblocking the issue for the 3.7 release branch.",
  "url": "https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/17384"
}

{
  "content": "# Investigation Report\n\n## Summary\n\nRemote-write queue resharding stalls because commit `184c7eb` moved `dataIn` tracking from the `WriteStorage`-level `timestampTracker.Commit()` (which runs unconditionally at scrape commit time) into `shards.enqueue()` (which blocks when queues are full). This causes the measured incoming data rate (`dataIn`) to be artificially capped at the outgoing rate (`dataOut`), preventing `calculateDesiredShards()` from ever computing a higher shard count. The same commit also removed the `dataDropped` EWMA and `dataKeptRatio` from the shard calculation, and replaced the `WriteStorage`-shared `highestRecvTimestamp` with a per-queue `highestTimestamp` metric updated inside `enqueue()`, compounding the problem.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File:** `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`\n**Functions:** `shards.enqueue()` (line 1312), `calculateDesiredShards()` (line 1111)\n**Commit:** `184c7eb9` (\"storage/remote: compute highestTimestamp and dataIn at QueueManager level\")\n\n### Mechanism\n\nPrior to the change, the data flow for shard calculation worked as follows:\n\n1. **`dataIn` tracked at `WriteStorage` level:** `timestampTracker.Commit()` in `write.go` called `rws.samplesIn.incr()` every scrape cycle, unconditionally. This `samplesIn` EWMA was shared across all `QueueManager` instances and ticked by a dedicated `WriteStorage.run()` goroutine.\n\n2. **`highestRecvTimestamp` tracked at `WriteStorage` level:** Set in `timestampTracker.Commit()` to the highest timestamp from the scrape, regardless of whether samples were enqueued.\n\n3. **`dataDropped` tracked in `Append()`:** When a series was filtered by relabeling, `dataDropped.incr(1)` was called, and `calculateDesiredShards()` used a `dataKeptRatio = dataOutRate / (dataDropped.rate() + dataOutRate)` to adjust the incoming rate.\n\nThe commit `184c7eb` changed this to:\n\n1. **`dataIn` moved into `shards.enqueue()` (line 1338):** `s.qm.dataIn.incr(1)` is called only when a sample is **successfully** enqueued into a shard queue.\n\n2. **`highestTimestamp` moved into `shards.enqueue()` (line 1337):** `s.qm.metrics.highestTimestamp.Set()` is called only upon successful enqueue.\n\n3. **`dataDropped` removed entirely:** The `dataKeptRatio` calculation was eliminated from `calculateDesiredShards()`.\n\n4. **`dataIn.tick()` moved into `calculateDesiredShards()` (line 1112):** Instead of being ticked by an independent goroutine in `WriteStorage.run()`, it's now ticked only when the shard calculation runs.\n\n### The Deadlock/Stall\n\nThe critical problem is in step 1. When the `Append()` method (line 726) tries to enqueue a sample, the flow is:\n\n```\nAppend() -> shards.enqueue() -> queues[shard].Append() -> if full, return false\n```\n\nWhen `enqueue()` returns false (queue full), `Append()` enters a backoff-retry loop (lines 756-780). During this blocking period:\n\n- **`dataIn` is NOT incremented** because `enqueue()` only calls `dataIn.incr(1)` on successful enqueue (line 1338).\n- The rate at which `dataIn` is incremented is therefore **bounded by the rate at which shards drain their queues** (i.e., `dataOut`).\n- When `calculateDesiredShards()` runs, it sees `dataInRate ~= dataOutRate`, computes `dataPendingRate ~= 0`, and `desiredShards ~= current shards`.\n- The `highestTimestamp` metric also stalls because it's only updated on successful enqueue, so `delay` (line 1127) also underestimates the backlog.\n\nThis creates a **feedback loop**: queues are full -> dataIn can't be measured accurately -> resharding doesn't trigger -> queues stay full.\n\n### Why It's Intermittent\n\nThe issue manifests when:\n\n1. **Target discovery changes** cause a burst of new series, increasing the scrape rate beyond current shard capacity.\n2. **Queue capacity fills up** (controlled by `queue_config.capacity`, default 10000 with `max_samples_per_send` of 500 = 20 batch slots).\n3. The timing depends on the rate of incoming samples vs. current shard throughput. If samples arrive slowly enough that queues never fill completely, resharding works correctly because `enqueue()` succeeds and `dataIn` reflects the true rate.\n4. The stall is more likely with **relabeled endpoints** that only accept a subset of series, because the old `dataKeptRatio` compensation was also removed.\n\nThe 30% tolerance band (`shardToleranceFraction = 0.3`, line 61) can mask small discrepancies, but once queues are saturated, the measured `dataInRate` becomes exactly `dataOutRate`, and `desiredShards` stays within the tolerance band of `numShards`.\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Code References (local working tree matches Sourcegraph HEAD)\n\n- **`shards.enqueue()`** - `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1312-1339`: `dataIn.incr(1)` at line 1338 only executes on successful enqueue. If `queues[shard].Append(data)` returns false (line 1321), the function returns false without incrementing `dataIn`.\n\n- **`QueueManager.Append()`** - `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:726-782`: Retry loop at line 756 blocks with exponential backoff when `enqueue()` returns false. During blocking, no `dataIn` increments occur.\n\n- **`calculateDesiredShards()`** - `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1111-1182`: Uses `dataInRate` (line 1121) which is now only incremented inside `enqueue()`. The formula `desiredShards = timePerSample * (dataInRate + backlogCatchup)` at line 1140 will underestimate when `dataInRate` is capped.\n\n- **`highestTimestamp` tracking** - `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1337`: `s.qm.metrics.highestTimestamp.Set(float64(data.timestamp / 1000))` only fires on successful enqueue, so the `delay` calculation at line 1127 (`highestRecv - highestSent`) also underestimates the true backlog.\n\n- **`updateShardsLoop()`** - `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1098-1123`: Runs every `shardUpdateDuration` (10s). Calls `calculateDesiredShards()` and `shouldReshard()`. When the calculated desired shards equals current shards, resharding is skipped.\n\n- **`reshardLoop()`** - `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1227-1242`: Receives on `reshardChan`, calls `shards.stop()` then `shards.start(numShards)`. During `stop()`, `softShutdown` is closed (line 1275) causing `enqueue()` to return false, which triggers `Append()` retry loops.\n\n- **Removed `dataDropped`** - The `dataDropped` EWMA and `dataKeptRatio` were removed in commit `184c7eb`. Previously `calculateDesiredShards()` at line 1123 used `dataKeptRatio = dataOutRate / (t.dataDropped.rate() + dataOutRate)` to account for relabel-filtered series. Without this, `dataInRate` (which now only counts enqueued samples) is compared directly to `dataOutRate`.\n\n- **Removed shared `samplesIn`** - `storage/remote/write.go:60-78`: The `WriteStorage` struct no longer has a `samplesIn` field or a `run()` goroutine to tick it. The `timestampTracker.Commit()` at line 331 no longer increments any per-QueueManager EWMA.\n\n### Commit History\n\n| Commit | Description | Impact |\n|--------|-------------|--------|\n| `184c7eb` | \"storage/remote: compute highestTimestamp and dataIn at QueueManager level\" | **Root cause**: Moved `dataIn` and `highestTimestamp` into `enqueue()`, removed `dataDropped`, removed shared `samplesIn` EWMA |\n| `ba14bc49` | \"chore: deprecate prometheus_remote_storage_{samples,exemplars,histograms}_in_total...\" | Deprecated old WriteStorage-level metrics that were the previous source of truth |\n| `6806b68` (release-3.7 only) | \"fix: Remote-write: revert changes in the queue resharding logic\" | Reverts both commits above on the release branch, restoring correct behavior |\n\n### GitHub Issue\n\n- **Issue [#17384](https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/17384)**: Reports instances lagging >1 hour after upgrade, shard count stuck at 3-4 despite low resource utilization. Confirmed as caused by `dataIn` being capped at `dataOut` rate.\n\n- **PR [#17412](https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/pull/17412)**: Reverts the problematic changes on the `release-3.7` branch.\n\n## Affected Components\n\n| Package/Module | File | Impact |\n|---------------|------|--------|\n| `storage/remote` | `queue_manager.go` | Core resharding logic: `calculateDesiredShards()`, `shards.enqueue()`, `updateShardsLoop()` |\n| `storage/remote` | `write.go` | `WriteStorage` no longer provides shared `samplesIn` EWMA or runs tick goroutine; `timestampTracker.Commit()` no longer feeds QueueManager dataIn |\n| `storage/remote` | `ewma.go` | EWMA rate tracking (`ewmaRate.incr()` / `.tick()` / `.rate()`) \u2014 behavior unchanged but inputs are now wrong |\n| Dashboards/Alerts | `documentation/prometheus-mixin/` | Alert `PrometheusRemoteWriteBehind` was updated to use new `queue_highest_timestamp_seconds` which also stalls |\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\nThe fix (already applied on `release-3.7` via commit `6806b68`) is to revert commits `184c7eb` and `ba14bc49` on `main`. This restores:\n\n1. **`dataIn` tracking at `WriteStorage.timestampTracker.Commit()`** \u2014 incremented unconditionally on every scrape commit, giving an accurate incoming sample rate independent of queue state.\n2. **Shared `samplesIn` EWMA with dedicated tick goroutine** \u2014 ensuring the rate is computed on a regular interval regardless of queue saturation.\n3. **`dataDropped` EWMA and `dataKeptRatio`** \u2014 accounting for relabel-filtered series in the shard calculation.\n4. **`highestRecvTimestamp` at `WriteStorage` level** \u2014 providing accurate backlog delay measurement.\n\nIf the per-queue metrics goal from PR #17065 is to be preserved, the correct approach would be to track `dataIn` at a point **before** the blocking enqueue \u2014 for example, incrementing `dataIn` inside `Append()` before the retry loop, or maintaining the `WriteStorage`-level EWMA while also providing per-queue metrics for observability.\n\n### Diagnostic Steps to Confirm\n\n1. **Check `prometheus_remote_storage_shards_desired` gauge**: If stuck at or near `prometheus_remote_storage_shards` despite growing backlog, the shard calculation is being starved of accurate input rate data.\n\n2. **Compare `prometheus_remote_storage_queue_highest_timestamp_seconds` vs `prometheus_remote_storage_highest_timestamp_in_seconds`**: If the queue-level metric lags significantly behind the storage-level metric, it confirms that `highestTimestamp` updates are blocked by full queues.\n\n3. **Check `prometheus_remote_storage_enqueue_retries_total`**: A rapidly increasing counter confirms that `Append()` is frequently blocked in its retry loop, meaning `enqueue()` is returning false and `dataIn` is not being incremented.\n\n4. **Check `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending`**: If stuck at a high value with no progress (not increasing or decreasing), shards are saturated but no resharding is occurring.\n\n5. **Enable debug logging** and look for `QueueManager.calculateDesiredShards` log lines: `dataInRate` approximately equal to `dataOutRate` with `dataPending` near zero despite known backlog confirms the feedback loop.\n\n6. **Monitor `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_dropped_total` with reason `unintentionally_dropped_series`**: High values indicate samples are being lost during the stall.\n",

        Code Changes (1)
        
1. WRITE /logs/agent/investigation.md
# Investigation Report

## Summary

Remote-write queue resharding stalls because commit `184c7eb` moved `dataIn` tracking from the `WriteStorage`-level `timestampTracker.Commit()` (which runs unconditionally at scrape commit time) into `shards.enqueue()` (which blocks when queues are full). This causes the measured incoming data rate (`dataIn`) to be artificially capped at the outgoing rate (`dataOut`), preventing `calculateDesiredShards()` from ever computing a higher shard count. The same commit also removed the `dataDropped` EWMA and `dataKeptRatio` from the shard calculation, and replaced the `WriteStorage`-shared `highestRecvTimestamp` with a per-queue `highestTimestamp` metric updated inside `enqueue()`, compounding the problem.

## Root Cause

**File:** `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`
**Functions:** `shards.enqueue()` (line 1312), `calculateDesiredShards()` (line 1111)
**Commit:** `184c7eb9` ("storage/remote: compute highestTimestamp and dataIn at QueueManager level")

### Mechanism

Prior to the change, the data flow for shard calculation worked as follows:

1. **`dataIn` tracked at `WriteStorage` level:** `timestampTracker.Commit()` in `write.go` called `rws.samplesIn.incr()` every scrape cycle, unconditionally. This `samplesIn` EWMA was shared across all `QueueManager` instances and ticked by a dedicated `WriteStorage.run()` goroutine.

2. **`highestRecvTimestamp` tracked at `WriteStorage` level:** Set in `timestampTracker.Commit()` to the highest timestamp from the scrape, regardless of whether samples were enqueued.

3. **`dataDropped` tracked in `Append()`:** When a series was filtered by relabeling, `dataDropped.incr(1)` was called, and `calculateDesiredShards()` used a `dataKeptRatio = dataOutRate / (dataDropped.rate() + dataOutRate)` to adjust the inco
... (truncated)
